German and Austro-Hungarian diplomats, however, scored a coup by persuading Bulgaria to join the attack on Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid2YqjfHLyyj8C_241–]_119-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid2YqjfHLyyj8C_241%E2%80%93]-119">[107]</a></sup> The Austro-Hungarian provinces of [Slovenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slovenia "Slovenia"), Croatia and [Bosnia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnia_(region) "Bosnia (region)") provided troops for Austria-Hungary in the fight with Serbia, Russia and Italy. Montenegro allied itself with Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeiberg200554–55_120-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeiberg200554%E2%80%9355-120">[108]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Bulgaria_southern_front.jpg/200px-Bulgaria_southern_front.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bulgaria_southern_front.jpg)

Bulgarian soldiers in a trench, preparing to fire against an incoming aeroplane

Bulgaria declared war on Serbia on 14 October 1915 and joined in the attack by the Austro-Hungarian army under Mackensen's army of 250,000 that was already underway. Serbia was conquered in a little more than a month, as the Central Powers, now including Bulgaria, sent in 600,000 troops in total. The Serbian army, fighting on two fronts and facing certain defeat, retreated into northern [Albania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principality_of_Albania "Principality of Albania"). The Serbs suffered defeat in the [Battle of Kosovo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo_offensive_(1915) "Kosovo offensive (1915)"). Montenegro covered the Serbian retreat toward the Adriatic coast in the [Battle of Mojkovac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Mojkovac "Battle of Mojkovac") on 6–7 January 1916, but ultimately the Austrians also conquered Montenegro. The surviving Serbian soldiers were then evacuated to Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts20051075–1076_121-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts20051075%E2%80%931076-121">[109]</a></sup> After the conquest, Serbia was divided between Austro-Hungary and Bulgaria.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiNardo2015102_122-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiNardo2015102-122">[110]</a></sup>

In late 1915, a Franco-British force landed at [Salonica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thessaloniki "Thessaloniki") in Greece to offer assistance and to pressure its government to declare war against the Central Powers. However, the pro-German [King Constantine I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_I_of_Greece "Constantine I of Greece") dismissed the pro-Allied government of [Eleftherios Venizelos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eleftherios_Venizelos "Eleftherios Venizelos") before the Allied expeditionary force arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeiberg2005108–110_123-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeiberg2005108%E2%80%93110-123">[111]</a></sup>

The Macedonian front was at first mostly static. French and Serbian forces retook limited areas of Macedonia by recapturing [Bitola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bitola "Bitola") on 19 November 1916 following the costly [Monastir offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monastir_offensive "Monastir offensive"), which brought stabilisation of the front.<sup id="cite_ref-124"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-124">[112]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Austrians_executing_Serbs_1917.JPG/220px-Austrians_executing_Serbs_1917.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Austrians_executing_Serbs_1917.JPG)

Austro-Hungarian troops executing captured Serbians, 1917. [Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia "Kingdom of Serbia") lost about 850,000 people during the war, a quarter of its pre-war population.<sup id="cite_ref-125"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-125">[113]</a></sup>

Serbian and French troops finally made a breakthrough in September 1918 in the [Vardar offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vardar_offensive "Vardar offensive"), after most German and Austro-Hungarian troops had been withdrawn. The Bulgarians were defeated at the [Battle of Dobro Pole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Dobro_Pole "Battle of Dobro Pole"), and by 25 September British and French troops had crossed the border into Bulgaria proper as the Bulgarian army collapsed. Bulgaria capitulated four days later, on 29 September 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerWoodMurphy1999150–152_126-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerWoodMurphy1999150%E2%80%93152-126">[114]</a></sup> The German high command responded by despatching troops to hold the line, but these forces were too weak to re-establish a front.<sup id="cite_ref-militera_127-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-militera-127">[115]</a></sup>

The disappearance of the Macedonian front meant that the road to [Budapest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Budapest "Budapest") and Vienna was now opened to Allied forces. Hindenburg and Ludendorff concluded that the strategic and operational balance had now shifted decidedly against the [Central Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers "Central Powers") and, a day after the Bulgarian collapse, insisted on an immediate peace settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoughty2005491_128-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoughty2005491-128">[116]</a></sup>

#### Ottoman Empire

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Scene_just_before_the_evacuation_at_Anzac._Australian_troops_charging_near_a_Turkish_trench._When_they_got_there_the..._-_NARA_-_533108.jpg/220px-Scene_just_before_the_evacuation_at_Anzac._Australian_troops_charging_near_a_Turkish_trench._When_they_got_there_the..._-_NARA_-_533108.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Scene_just_before_the_evacuation_at_Anzac._Australian_troops_charging_near_a_Turkish_trench._When_they_got_there_the..._-_NARA_-_533108.jpg)

Australian troops charging near a Turkish trench during the [Gallipoli campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gallipoli_campaign "Gallipoli campaign")

The Ottomans threatened Russia's [Caucasian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus "Caucasus") territories and Britain's communications with India via the [Suez Canal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Canal "Suez Canal"). As the conflict progressed, the Ottoman Empire took advantage of the European powers' preoccupation with the war and conducted large-scale ethnic cleansing of the indigenous [Armenian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenians "Armenians"), [Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greeks "Greeks"), and [Assyrian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assyrian_people "Assyrian people") Christian populations, known as the [Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide "Armenian genocide"), [Greek genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_genocide "Greek genocide"), and [Sayfo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sayfo "Sayfo") respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-129"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-129">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-130">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lieberman_131-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-lieberman-131">[119]</a></sup>

The British and French opened overseas fronts with the [Gallipoli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gallipoli_campaign "Gallipoli campaign") (1915) and [Mesopotamian campaigns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamian_campaign "Mesopotamian campaign") (1914). In Gallipoli, the Ottoman Empire successfully repelled the British, French, and [Australian and New Zealand Army Corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australian_and_New_Zealand_Army_Corps "Australian and New Zealand Army Corps") (ANZACs). In [Mesopotamia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamia "Mesopotamia"), by contrast, after the defeat of the British defenders in the [siege of Kut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Kut "Siege of Kut") by the Ottomans (1915–16), British Imperial forces reorganised and captured [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad") in March 1917. The British were aided in Mesopotamia by local Arab and Assyrian fighters, while the Ottomans employed local [Kurdish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurds "Kurds") and [Turcoman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_Turkmen "Iraqi Turkmen") tribes.<sup id="cite_ref-132"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-132">[120]</a></sup>

Further to the west, the [Suez Canal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Canal "Suez Canal") was defended from Ottoman attacks in 1915 and 1916; in August 1916, a German and Ottoman force was defeated at the [Battle of Romani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Romani "Battle of Romani") by the [ANZAC Mounted Division](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ANZAC_Mounted_Division "ANZAC Mounted Division") and the [52nd (Lowland) Infantry Division](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/52nd_(Lowland)_Infantry_Division "52nd (Lowland) Infantry Division"). Following this victory, an [Egyptian Expeditionary Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_Expeditionary_Force "Egyptian Expeditionary Force") advanced across the [Sinai Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula "Sinai Peninsula"), pushing Ottoman forces back in the [Battle of Magdhaba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Magdhaba "Battle of Magdhaba") in December and the [Battle of Rafa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Rafa "Battle of Rafa") on the border between the Egyptian [Sinai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula "Sinai Peninsula") and Ottoman Palestine in January 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-133"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-133">[121]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Sarikam.jpg/220px-Sarikam.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sarikam.jpg)

Russian forest trench at the [Battle of Sarikamish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Sarikamish "Battle of Sarikamish"), 1914–1915

Russian armies generally had success in the [Caucasus campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus_campaign "Caucasus campaign"). [Enver Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enver_Pasha "Enver Pasha"), supreme commander of the Ottoman armed forces, was ambitious and dreamed of re-conquering central Asia and areas that had been previously lost to Russia. He was, however, a poor commander.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFromkin2004119_134-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFromkin2004119-134">[122]</a></sup> He launched an offensive against the Russians in the Caucasus in December 1914 with 100,000 troops, insisting on a frontal attack against mountainous Russian positions in winter. He lost 86% of his force at the [Battle of Sarikamish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Sarikamish "Battle of Sarikamish").<sup id="cite_ref-caven_135-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-caven-135">[123]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Ottoman_15th_Corps.jpg/220px-Ottoman_15th_Corps.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ottoman_15th_Corps.jpg)

Kaiser Wilhelm II and [Prince Leopold of Bavaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_Leopold_of_Bavaria "Prince Leopold of Bavaria") inspecting Turkish troops of the 15th Corps in East Galicia, Austria-Hungary (now Poland).

The Ottoman Empire, with German support, invaded Persia (modern [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran "Iran")) in December 1914 to cut off British and Russian access to [petroleum reservoirs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petroleum_reservoir "Petroleum reservoir") around [Baku](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baku "Baku") near the [Caspian Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_Sea "Caspian Sea").<sup id="cite_ref-136"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-136">[124]</a></sup> Persia, ostensibly neutral, had long been under the spheres of British and Russian influence. The Ottomans and Germans were aided by [Kurdish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurds "Kurds") and [Azeri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijanis "Azerbaijanis") forces, together with a large number of major Iranian tribes, such as the [Qashqai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qashqai_people "Qashqai people"), [Tangistanis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tangestan_County "Tangestan County"), [Lurs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lurs "Lurs"), and [Khamseh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khamseh "Khamseh"), while the Russians and British had the support of Armenian and Assyrian forces. The [Persian campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_campaign_(World_War_I) "Persian campaign (World War I)") was to last until 1918 and end in failure for the Ottomans and their allies. However, the Russian withdrawal from the war in 1917 led Armenian and Assyrian forces, who had hitherto inflicted a series of defeats upon the forces of the Ottomans and their allies, to be cut off from supply lines, outnumbered, outgunned and isolated, forcing them to fight and flee towards British lines in northern Mesopotamia.<sup id="cite_ref-137"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-137">[125]</a></sup>

General [Yudenich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolai_Yudenich "Nikolai Yudenich"), the Russian commander from 1915 to 1916, drove the Turks out of most of the southern [Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus "Caucasus") with a string of victories.<sup id="cite_ref-caven_135-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-caven-135">[123]</a></sup>

The [Arab Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Revolt "Arab Revolt"), instigated by the Arab bureau of the British [Foreign Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign,_Commonwealth_and_Development_Office "Foreign, Commonwealth and Development Office"), started in June 1916 with the [Battle of Mecca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Mecca_(1916) "Battle of Mecca (1916)"), led by [Sharif Hussein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_Sharif_of_Mecca "Hussein bin Ali, Sharif of Mecca") of [Mecca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecca "Mecca"). The Sharif declared the independence of the [Kingdom of Hejaz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hejaz "Kingdom of Hejaz") and, with British assistance, conquered much of Ottoman-held Arabia, resulting finally in the Ottoman surrender of Damascus. [Fakhri Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fakhri_Pasha "Fakhri Pasha"), the Ottoman commander of [Medina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medina "Medina"), resisted for more than 2+1⁄2 years during the [siege of Medina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Medina "Siege of Medina") before surrendering in January 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESachar1970122–138_138-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTESachar1970122%E2%80%93138-138">[126]</a></sup>

The [Senussi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senusiyya "Senusiyya") tribe, along the border of [Italian Libya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Libya "Italian Libya") and [British Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Egypt "British Egypt"), incited and armed by the Turks, waged a small-scale [guerrilla war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare "Guerrilla warfare") against Allied troops. The British were forced to dispatch 12,000 troops to oppose them in the [Senussi campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senussi_campaign "Senussi campaign"). Their rebellion was finally crushed in mid-1916.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994_139-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994-139">[127]</a></sup>

Total Allied casualties on the Ottoman fronts amounted to 650,000 men. Total Ottoman casualties were 725,000, with 325,000 dead and 400,000 wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-Brief_Ottoman_History_140-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Brief_Ottoman_History-140">[128]</a></sup>

#### Italian Front

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Italian_Front_1915-1917.jpg/220px-Italian_Front_1915-1917.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Italian_Front_1915-1917.jpg)

[Isonzo Offensives 1915–1917](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_the_Isonzo "Battles of the Isonzo")

Though Italy joined the Triple Alliance in 1882, a treaty with its traditional Austrian enemy was so controversial that subsequent governments denied its existence and the terms were only made public in 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson200913_141-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson200913-141">[129]</a></sup> This arose from [nationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_nationalism "Italian nationalism") designs on Austro-Hungarian territory in [Trentino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trentino "Trentino"), the [Austrian Littoral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrian_Littoral "Austrian Littoral"), [Rijeka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rijeka "Rijeka") and [Dalmatia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalmatia "Dalmatia"), which were considered vital to secure the borders established in [1866](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Italian_War_of_Independence "Third Italian War of Independence").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson20099–10_142-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson20099%E2%80%9310-142">[130]</a></sup> In 1902, Rome secretly had agreed with France to remain neutral if the latter was attacked by Germany, effectively nullifying its role in the Triple Alliance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGardner2015120_143-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGardner2015120-143">[131]</a></sup>

When the war began in 1914, Italy argued the Triple Alliance was defensive and it was not obliged to support an Austrian attack on Serbia. Opposition to joining the Central Powers increased when Turkey became a member in September, since in [1911](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italo-Turkish_War "Italo-Turkish War") Italy had occupied Ottoman possessions in [Libya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Libya "Italian Libya") and the [Dodecanese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dodecanese "Dodecanese") islands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson200914_144-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson200914-144">[132]</a></sup> To secure Italian neutrality, the Central Powers offered them [Tunisia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_protectorate_of_Tunisia "French protectorate of Tunisia"), while in return for an immediate entry into the war, the Allies agreed to their demands for Austrian territory and sovereignty over the Dodecanese.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson200930–31_145-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson200930%E2%80%9331-145">[133]</a></sup> Although they remained secret, these provisions were incorporated into the April 1915 [Treaty of London](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_London_(1915) "Treaty of London (1915)"); Italy joined the Triple Entente and, on 23 May, declared war on Austria-Hungary,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994166_146-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994166-146">[134]</a></sup> followed by Germany fifteen months later.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/1917_ortler_vorgipfelstellung_3850_m_highest_trench_in_history_of_first_world_war.jpg/220px-1917_ortler_vorgipfelstellung_3850_m_highest_trench_in_history_of_first_world_war.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1917_ortler_vorgipfelstellung_3850_m_highest_trench_in_history_of_first_world_war.jpg)

Austro-Hungarian trench at 3,850 metres in the [Ortler Alps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ortler_Alps "Ortler Alps"), one of the most challenging fronts of the war

The pre-1914 Italian army was short of officers, trained men, adequate transport and modern weapons; by April 1915, some of these deficiencies had been remedied but it was still unprepared for the major offensive required by the Treaty of London.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson200957_147-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson200957-147">[135]</a></sup> The advantage of superior numbers was offset by the difficult terrain; much of the fighting took place high in the [Alps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alps "Alps") and [Dolomites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dolomites "Dolomites"), where trench lines had to be cut through rock and ice and keeping troops supplied was a major challenge. These issues were exacerbated by unimaginative strategies and tactics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshallJosephy1982108_148-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshallJosephy1982108-148">[136]</a></sup> Between 1915 and 1917, the Italian commander, [Luigi Cadorna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luigi_Cadorna "Luigi Cadorna"), undertook [a series of frontal assaults along the Isonzo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_the_Isonzo "Battles of the Isonzo"), which made little progress and cost many lives; by the end of the war, Italian combat deaths totalled around 548,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFornassin201739–62_149-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFornassin201739%E2%80%9362-149">[137]</a></sup>

In the spring of 1916, the Austro-Hungarians counterattacked in [Asiago](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asiago "Asiago") in the _[Strafexpedition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Asiago "Battle of Asiago")_, but made little progress and were pushed by the Italians back to Tyrol.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson2009163_150-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson2009163-150">[138]</a></sup> Although an Italian corps occupied southern [Albania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albania_during_World_War_I "Albania during World War I") in May 1916, their main focus was the Isonzo front which, after the [capture of Gorizia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Doberd%C3%B2 "Battle of Doberdò") in August 1916, remained static until October 1917. After a combined Austro-German force won a major victory at [Caporetto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Caporetto "Battle of Caporetto"), Cadorna was replaced by [Armando Diaz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armando_Diaz "Armando Diaz") who retreated more than 100 kilometres (62 mi) before holding positions along the [Piave River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_the_Piave_River "Second Battle of the Piave River").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994317_151-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994317-151">[139]</a></sup> A second Austrian [offensive was repulsed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_the_Piave_River "Second Battle of the Piave River") in June 1918 and by October it was clear the Central Powers had lost the war. On 24 October, Diaz launched the [Battle of Vittorio Veneto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Vittorio_Veneto "Battle of Vittorio Veneto") and initially met stubborn resistance,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994482_152-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994482-152">[140]</a></sup> but with Austria-Hungary collapsing, Hungarian divisions in Italy demanded they be sent home.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994484_153-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994484-153">[141]</a></sup> When this was granted, many others followed and the Imperial army disintegrated, the Italians taking over 300,000 prisoners.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson2009364_154-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson2009364-154">[142]</a></sup> On 3 November, the [Armistice of Villa Giusti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice_of_Villa_Giusti "Armistice of Villa Giusti") ended hostilities between Austria-Hungary and Italy which occupied [Trieste](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trieste "Trieste") and areas along the [Adriatic Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adriatic_Sea "Adriatic Sea") awarded to it in 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994491_155-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994491-155">[143]</a></sup>

### Eastern Front

#### Initial actions

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Mikolaj_II_w_Twierdzy_Przemysl.jpg/220px-Mikolaj_II_w_Twierdzy_Przemysl.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mikolaj_II_w_Twierdzy_Przemysl.jpg)

Emperor [Nicholas II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia "Nicholas II of Russia") and [Grand Duke Nikolaevich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duke_Nicholas_Nikolaevich_of_Russia_(1856%E2%80%931929) "Grand Duke Nicholas Nikolaevich of Russia (1856–1929)") following the Russian [capture of Przemyśl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Przemy%C5%9Bl "Siege of Przemyśl"), the longest siege of the war.

As previously agreed with France, Russian plans at the start of the war were to simultaneously advance into [Austrian Galicia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia_and_Lodomeria "Kingdom of Galicia and Lodomeria") and East Prussia as soon as possible. Although their [attack on Galicia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Galicia "Battle of Galicia") was largely successful, and the invasions achieved their aim of forcing Germany to divert troops from the Western Front, the speed of mobilisation meant they did so without much of their heavy equipment and support functions. These weaknesses contributed to Russian defeats at [Tannenberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Tannenberg "Battle of Tannenberg") and the [Masurian Lakes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Battle_of_the_Masurian_Lakes "First Battle of the Masurian Lakes") in August and September 1914, forcing them to withdraw from East Prussia with heavy losses.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005715_156-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005715-156">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeyer2006152–154,_161,_163,_175,_182_157-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeyer2006152%E2%80%93154,_161,_163,_175,_182-157">[145]</a></sup> By spring 1915, they had also retreated from Galicia, and the May 1915 [Gorlice–Tarnów offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorlice%E2%80%93Tarn%C3%B3w_offensive "Gorlice–Tarnów offensive") allowed the Central Powers to invade [Russian-occupied Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_Poland "Congress Poland").<sup id="cite_ref-Smele_158-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Smele-158">[146]</a></sup>

Despite the successful June 1916 [Brusilov offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brusilov_offensive "Brusilov offensive") against the Austrians in eastern Galicia,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchindler2003?_159-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchindler2003?-159">[147]</a></sup> shortages of supplies, heavy losses and command failures prevented the Russians from fully exploiting their victory. However, it was one of the most significant offensives of the war, diverting German resources from [Verdun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Verdun "Battle of Verdun"), relieving Austro-Hungarian pressure on the Italians, and convincing Romania to enter the war on the side of the Allies on 27 August. It also fatally weakened both the Austrian and Russian armies, whose offensive capabilities were badly affected by their losses and increased disillusion with the war that ultimately led to the Russian revolutions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETucker2002119_160-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETucker2002119-160">[148]</a></sup>

Meanwhile, unrest grew in Russia as [the Tsar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia "Nicholas II of Russia") remained at the front, with the home front controlled by [Empress Alexandra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexandra_Feodorovna_(Alix_of_Hesse) "Alexandra Feodorovna (Alix of Hesse)"). Her increasingly incompetent rule and food shortages in urban areas led to widespread protests and the murder of her favourite, [Grigori Rasputin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grigori_Rasputin "Grigori Rasputin"), at the end of 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-161"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-161">[149]</a></sup>

#### Romanian participation

Romania key locations 1916–1918 (note; using 2022 borders)

Despite secretly agreeing to support the Triple Alliance in 1883, Romania increasingly found itself at odds with the Central Powers over their support for Bulgaria in the Balkan Wars and the status of ethnic Romanian communities in [Hungarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary "Kingdom of Hungary")\-controlled [Transylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transylvania "Transylvania"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJelavich1992441–442_162-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJelavich1992441%E2%80%93442-162">[150]</a></sup> which comprised an estimated 2.8 million of the 5.0 million population.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDumitru2012171_163-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDumitru2012171-163">[151]</a></sup> With the ruling elite split into pro-German and pro-Entente factions, Romania remained neutral in 1914, arguing like Italy that because Austria-Hungary had declared war on Serbia, it was under no obligation to join them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDumitru2012170_164-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDumitru2012170-164">[152]</a></sup> They maintained this position for the next two years while allowing Germany and Austria to transport military supplies and advisors across Romanian territory.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994282_165-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994282-165">[153]</a></sup>

In September 1914, Russia acknowledged Romanian rights to Austro-Hungarian territories including Transylvania and [Banat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banat "Banat"), whose acquisition had widespread popular support,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDumitru2012171_163-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDumitru2012171-163">[151]</a></sup> and Russian success against Austria led Romania to join the Entente in the August 1916 [Treaty of Bucharest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Bucharest_(1916) "Treaty of Bucharest (1916)").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994282_165-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994282-165">[153]</a></sup> Under the strategic plan known as [Hypothesis Z](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypothesis_Z "Hypothesis Z"), the Romanian army planned an offensive into Transylvania, while defending Southern [Dobruja](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dobruja "Dobruja") and [Giurgiu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giurgiu_County "Giurgiu County") against a possible Bulgarian counterattack.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETorrie19787–8_166-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETorrie19787%E2%80%938-166">[154]</a></sup> On 27 August 1916, they [attacked Transylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Transylvania "Battle of Transylvania") and occupied substantial parts of the province before being driven back by the recently formed [German 9th Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/9th_Army_(German_Empire) "9th Army (German Empire)"), led by former Chief of Staff [Erich von Falkenhayn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erich_von_Falkenhayn "Erich von Falkenhayn").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarrett201396–98_167-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarrett201396%E2%80%9398-167">[155]</a></sup> A combined German-Bulgarian-Turkish offensive captured Dobruja and Giurgiu, although the bulk of the Romanian army managed to escape encirclement and retreated to [Bucharest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bucharest "Bucharest"), which [surrendered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Bucharest "Battle of Bucharest") to the Central Powers on 6 December 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-168"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-168">[156]</a></sup>

In the summer of 1917, a Central Powers offensive began in Romania under the command of August von Mackensen to knock Romania out of the war, resulting in the battles of [Oituz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Battle_of_Oituz "Third Battle of Oituz"), [Mărăști](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_M%C4%83r%C4%83%C8%99ti "Battle of Mărăști") and [Mărășești](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_M%C4%83r%C4%83%C8%99e%C8%99ti "Battle of Mărășești") where up to 1,000,000 Central Powers troops were present. The battles lasted from 22 July to 3 September and eventually, the Romanian army was victorious advancing 500 km<sup>2</sup>. August von Mackensen could not plan for another offensive as he had to transfer troops to the Italian Front.<sup id="cite_ref-169"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-169">[157]</a></sup> Following the Russian revolution, Romania found itself alone on the Eastern Front and signed the [Treaty of Bucharest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Bucharest_(1918) "Treaty of Bucharest (1918)") with the Central Powers, which recognised Romanian sovereignty over [Bessarabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bessarabia "Bessarabia") in return for ceding control of passes in the Carpathian Mountains to Austria-Hungary and leasing its oil wells to Germany for 99 years. Although approved by [Parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliament_of_Romania "Parliament of Romania"), [King Ferdinand I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_Romania "Ferdinand I of Romania") refused to sign it, hoping for an Allied victory in the west.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrampton199424–25_170-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrampton199424%E2%80%9325-170">[158]</a></sup> Romania re-entered the war on 10 November 1918 on the side of the Allies and the Treaty of Bucharest was formally annulled by the Armistice of 11 November 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBéla1998429_171-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEB%C3%A9la1998429-171">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-173">[m]</a></sup>

### Central Powers peace overtures

On 12 December 1916, after ten brutal months of the [Battle of Verdun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Verdun "Battle of Verdun") and a [successful offensive against Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romania_in_World_War_I#The_counteroffensive_of_the_Central_Powers "Romania in World War I"), Germany attempted to negotiate a peace with the Allies.<sup id="cite_ref-lanoszka_174-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-lanoszka-174">[161]</a></sup> However, this attempt was rejected out of hand as a "duplicitous war ruse".<sup id="cite_ref-lanoszka_174-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-lanoszka-174">[161]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/River_Crossing_NGM-v31-p338.jpg/220px-River_Crossing_NGM-v31-p338.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:River_Crossing_NGM-v31-p338.jpg)

"_[They shall not pass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/They_shall_not_pass "They shall not pass")"_, a phrase typically associated with the defence of Verdun

US president [Woodrow Wilson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson "Woodrow Wilson") attempted to intervene as a peacemaker, asking for both sides to state their demands and start negotiations. [Lloyd George's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Lloyd_George "David Lloyd George") War Cabinet considered the German offer to be a ploy to create divisions among the Allies. After initial outrage and much deliberation, they took Wilson's note as a separate effort, signalling that the United States was on the verge of entering the war against Germany following the "submarine outrages". While the Allies debated a response to Wilson's offer, the Germans chose to rebuff it in favour of "a direct exchange of views". Learning of the German response, the Allied governments were free to make clear demands in their response of 14 January. They sought restoration of damages, the evacuation of occupied territories, reparations for France, Russia and Romania, and a recognition of the principle of nationalities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan1998345_175-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan1998345-175">[162]</a></sup> This included the liberation of Italians, Slavs, Romanians, Czecho-Slovaks, and the creation of a "free and united Poland".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan1998345_175-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan1998345-175">[162]</a></sup> The Allies sought guarantees that would prevent or limit future wars, complete with sanctions, as a condition of any peace settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKernek1970721–766_176-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKernek1970721%E2%80%93766-176">[163]</a></sup> The negotiations failed and the Entente powers rejected the German offer on the grounds of honour, and noted Germany had not put forward any specific proposals.<sup id="cite_ref-lanoszka_174-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-lanoszka-174">[161]</a></sup>

### Final years of the war

#### Russian Revolution and withdrawal

By the end of 1916, Russian casualties totalled nearly five million killed, wounded or captured, with major urban areas affected by food shortages and high prices. In March 1917, Tsar Nicholas ordered the military to forcibly suppress a wave of strikes in [Petrograd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Petersburg "Saint Petersburg") but the troops refused to fire on the crowds. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeckett2007523_177-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeckett2007523-177">[164]</a></sup> Revolutionaries set up the [Petrograd Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petrograd_Soviet "Petrograd Soviet") and fearing a left-wing takeover, the [State Duma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_Duma "State Duma") forced Nicholas to abdicate and established the [Russian Provisional Government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government "Russian Provisional Government"), which confirmed Russia's willingness to continue the war. However, the Petrograd Soviet refused to disband, creating [competing power centres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dual_power "Dual power") and causing confusion and chaos, with frontline soldiers becoming increasingly demoralised and unwilling to fight on.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinter2014110–132_178-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinter2014110%E2%80%93132-178">[165]</a></sup>

Following the Tsar's abdication, [Vladimir Lenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin "Vladimir Lenin")—with the help of the German government—was ushered from Switzerland into Russia on 16 April 1917. Discontent and the weaknesses of the Provisional Government led to a rise in the popularity of the Bolshevik Party, led by Lenin, which demanded an immediate end to the war. The Revolution of November was followed in December by an armistice and negotiations with Germany. At first, the Bolsheviks refused the German terms, but when German troops began marching across Ukraine unopposed, the new government acceded to the [Treaty of Brest-Litovsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk "Treaty of Brest-Litovsk") on 3 March 1918. The treaty ceded vast territories, including Finland, Estonia, Latvia, Lithuania, and parts of Poland and Ukraine to the Central Powers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler-Bennett193836–41_179-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler-Bennett193836%E2%80%9341-179">[166]</a></sup>

With the [Russian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") out of the war, Romania found itself alone on the Eastern Front and signed the [Treaty of Bucharest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Bucharest_(1918) "Treaty of Bucharest (1918)") with the Central Powers in May 1918, ending the state of war between Romania and the [Central Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers "Central Powers"). Under the terms of the treaty, Romania had to give territory to Austria-Hungary and Bulgaria and lease its oil reserves to Germany. However, the terms also included the Central Powers' recognition of the union of [Bessarabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bessarabia "Bessarabia") with Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-180"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-180">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-181">[168]</a></sup>

#### United States enters the war

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/President_Woodrow_Wilson_asking_Congress_to_declare_war_on_Germany%2C_2_April_1917.jpg/220px-President_Woodrow_Wilson_asking_Congress_to_declare_war_on_Germany%2C_2_April_1917.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:President_Woodrow_Wilson_asking_Congress_to_declare_war_on_Germany,_2_April_1917.jpg)

[President Wilson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson "Woodrow Wilson") asking [Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress "United States Congress") to declare war on Germany, 2 April 1917

The United States was a major supplier of war material to the Allies but remained neutral in 1914, in large part due to domestic opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStevenson2012315–316_182-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStevenson2012315%E2%80%93316-182">[169]</a></sup> The most significant factor in creating the support Wilson needed was the German submarine offensive, which not only cost American lives but paralysed trade as ships were reluctant to put to sea.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStevenson2012317_183-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStevenson2012317-183">[170]</a></sup>

On 6 April 1917, Congress [declared war on Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_declaration_of_war_on_Germany_(1917) "United States declaration of war on Germany (1917)") as an "Associated Power" of the Allies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994318_184-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1994318-184">[171]</a></sup> The [United States Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Navy "United States Navy") sent a [battleship group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Battleship_Division_Nine_(World_War_I) "United States Battleship Division Nine (World War I)") to [Scapa Flow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scapa_Flow "Scapa Flow") to join the Grand Fleet, and provided convoy escorts. In April 1917, the [United States Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army "United States Army") had fewer than 300,000 men, including [National Guard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_National_Guard "Army National Guard") units, compared to British and French armies of 4.1 and 8.3 million respectively. The [Selective Service Act of 1917](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selective_Service_Act_of_1917 "Selective Service Act of 1917") drafted 2.8 million men, though training and equipping such numbers was a huge logistical challenge. By June 1918, over 667,000 members of the [American Expeditionary Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Expeditionary_Forces "American Expeditionary Forces") (AEF) were transported to France, a figure which reached 2 million by the end of November.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrotelueschen200614–15_185-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrotelueschen200614%E2%80%9315-185">[172]</a></sup>

Despite his conviction that Germany must be defeated, Wilson went to war to ensure the US played a leading role in shaping the peace, which meant preserving the AEF as a separate military force, rather than being absorbed into British or French units as his Allies wanted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStevenson2012318_186-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStevenson2012318-186">[173]</a></sup> He was strongly supported by AEF commander General [John J. Pershing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_J._Pershing "John J. Pershing"), a proponent of pre-1914 "open warfare" who considered the French and British emphasis on artillery as misguided and incompatible with American "offensive spirit".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrotelueschen200644–46_187-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrotelueschen200644%E2%80%9346-187">[174]</a></sup> Much to the frustration of his Allies, who had suffered heavy losses in 1917, he insisted on retaining control of American troops, and refused to commit them to the front line until able to operate as independent units. As a result, the first significant US involvement was the [Meuse–Argonne offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meuse%E2%80%93Argonne_offensive "Meuse–Argonne offensive") in late September 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStevenson2012403_188-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStevenson2012403-188">[175]</a></sup>

#### Nivelle Offensive (April–May 1917)

[![Files of soldiers with rifles slung follow close behind a tank, there is a dead body in the foreground](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Canadian_tank_and_soldiers_Vimy_1917.jpg/220px-Canadian_tank_and_soldiers_Vimy_1917.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Canadian_tank_and_soldiers_Vimy_1917.jpg)

[Canadian Corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canadian_Corps "Canadian Corps") troops at the [Battle of Vimy Ridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Vimy_Ridge "Battle of Vimy Ridge"), 1917

In December 1916, [Robert Nivelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Nivelle "Robert Nivelle") replaced Pétain as commander of French armies on the Western Front and began planning a [spring attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nivelle_offensive "Nivelle offensive") in [Champagne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Champagne_(province) "Champagne (province)"), part of a joint Franco-British operation. Nivelle claimed the capture of his main objective, the [Chemin des Dames](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemin_des_Dames "Chemin des Dames"), would achieve a massive breakthrough and cost no more than 15,000 casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayton2003124_189-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayton2003124-189">[176]</a></sup> Poor security meant German intelligence was well informed on tactics and timetables, but despite this, when the attack began on 16 April the French made substantial gains, before being brought to a halt by the newly built and extremely strong defences of the Hindenburg Line. Nivelle persisted with frontal assaults and, by 25 April, the French had suffered nearly 135,000 casualties, including 30,000 dead, most incurred in the first two days.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayton2003129_190-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayton2003129-190">[177]</a></sup>

Concurrent British attacks at [Arras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Arras_(1917) "Battle of Arras (1917)") were more successful, though ultimately of little strategic value.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStrachan2003244_191-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStrachan2003244-191">[178]</a></sup> Operating as a separate unit for the first time, the [Canadian Corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canadian_Corps "Canadian Corps") capture of [Vimy Ridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Vimy_Ridge "Battle of Vimy Ridge") is viewed by many Canadians as a defining moment in creating a sense of national identity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInglis19952_192-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInglis19952-192">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHumphries200766_193-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHumphries200766-193">[180]</a></sup> Though Nivelle continued the offensive, on 3 May the [21st Division](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/21st_Infantry_Division_(France) "21st Infantry Division (France)"), which had been involved in some of the heaviest fighting at Verdun, refused orders to go into battle, initiating the [French Army mutinies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1917_French_Army_mutinies "1917 French Army mutinies"); within days, "collective indiscipline" had spread to 54 divisions, while over 20,000 deserted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHorne1964323_194-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHorne1964323-194">[181]</a></sup> Unrest was almost entirely confined to the infantry, whose demands were largely non-political, including better economic support for families at home, and regular periods of leave, which Nivelle had ended.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayton2003131_195-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayton2003131-195">[182]</a></sup>

#### Sinai and Palestine campaign (1917–1918)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Capture_of_Jerusalem_1917d.jpg/220px-Capture_of_Jerusalem_1917d.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Capture_of_Jerusalem_1917d.jpg)

British artillery battery on [Mount Scopus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Scopus "Mount Scopus") in the [Battle of Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Jerusalem "Battle of Jerusalem"), 1917.

In March and April 1917, at the [First](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Battle_of_Gaza "First Battle of Gaza") and [Second Battles of Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Gaza "Second Battle of Gaza"), German and Ottoman forces stopped the advance of the Egyptian Expeditionary Force, which had begun in August 1916 at the Battle of Romani.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEErickson2001163_196-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErickson2001163-196">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-197">[184]</a></sup> At the end of October 1917, the [Sinai and Palestine campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinai_and_Palestine_campaign "Sinai and Palestine campaign") resumed, when General [Edmund Allenby](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edmund_Allenby,_1st_Viscount_Allenby "Edmund Allenby, 1st Viscount Allenby")'s [XXth Corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XX_Corps_(United_Kingdom) "XX Corps (United Kingdom)"), [XXI Corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XXI_Corps_(United_Kingdom) "XXI Corps (United Kingdom)") and [Desert Mounted Corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert_Mounted_Corps "Desert Mounted Corps") won the [Battle of Beersheba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Beersheba_(1917) "Battle of Beersheba (1917)").<sup id="cite_ref-198"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-198">[185]</a></sup> Two Ottoman armies were defeated a few weeks later at the [Battle of Mughar Ridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Mughar_Ridge "Battle of Mughar Ridge") and, early in December, [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem") had been captured following another Ottoman defeat at the [Battle of Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Jerusalem "Battle of Jerusalem").<sup id="cite_ref-199"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-199">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-200">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-201">[188]</a></sup> About this time, [Friedrich Freiherr Kress von Kressenstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Freiherr_Kress_von_Kressenstein "Friedrich Freiherr Kress von Kressenstein") was relieved of his duties as the Eighth Army's commander, replaced by [Djevad Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cevat_%C3%87obanl%C4%B1 "Cevat Çobanlı"), and a few months later the commander of the [Ottoman Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Military of the Ottoman Empire") in Palestine, [Erich von Falkenhayn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erich_von_Falkenhayn "Erich von Falkenhayn"), was replaced by [Otto Liman von Sanders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_Liman_von_Sanders "Otto Liman von Sanders").<sup id="cite_ref-202"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-202">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-203">[190]</a></sup>

In early 1918, the front line was [extended](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capture_of_Jericho "Capture of Jericho") and the [Jordan Valley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_occupation_of_the_Jordan_Valley "British occupation of the Jordan Valley") was occupied, following the [First Transjordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Transjordan_attack_on_Amman "First Transjordan attack on Amman") and the [Second Transjordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Transjordan_attack_on_Shunet_Nimrin_and_Es_Salt "Second Transjordan attack on Shunet Nimrin and Es Salt") attacks by British Empire forces in March and April 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEErickson2001195_204-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErickson2001195-204">[191]</a></sup>

#### German offensive and Allied counter-offensive (March–November 1918)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Riflemen-1918-Western-Front.png/220px-Riflemen-1918-Western-Front.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Riflemen-1918-Western-Front.png)

Between April and November 1918, the Allies increased their front-line rifle strength while German strength fell by half.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAyers1919104_205-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAyers1919104-205">[192]</a></sup>

In December 1917, the Central Powers signed an armistice with Russia, thus freeing large numbers of German troops for use in the West. With German reinforcements and new American troops pouring in, the outcome was to be decided on the Western Front. The Central Powers knew that they could not win a protracted war, but they held high hopes for success in a final quick offensive.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeyman1997146–147_206-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeyman1997146%E2%80%93147-206">[193]</a></sup> Ludendorff drew up plans ([codenamed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code_name "Code name") [Operation Michael](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Michael "Operation Michael")) for the 1918 offensive on the Western Front. The operation commenced on 21 March 1918, with an attack on British forces near [Saint-Quentin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint-Quentin,_Aisne "Saint-Quentin, Aisne"). German forces achieved an unprecedented advance of 60 kilometres (37 mi).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWestwell2004_207-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWestwell2004-207">[194]</a></sup> The initial offensive was a success; after heavy fighting, however, the offensive was halted. Lacking tanks or [motorised artillery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-propelled_artillery "Self-propelled artillery"), the Germans were unable to consolidate their gains. The problems of re-supply were also exacerbated by increasing distances that now stretched over terrain that was shell-torn and often impassable to traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGray199186_208-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGray199186-208">[195]</a></sup>

Following this, Germany launched [Operation Georgette](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Lys_(1918) "Battle of the Lys (1918)") against the northern [English Channel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Channel "English Channel") ports. The Allies halted the drive after limited territorial gains by Germany. The German Army to the south then conducted [Operations Blücher and Yorck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Battle_of_the_Aisne "Third Battle of the Aisne"), pushing broadly towards Paris. Germany launched Operation Marne ([Second Battle of the Marne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Battle_of_the_Marne "Second Battle of the Marne")) on 15 July, in an attempt to encircle [Reims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reims "Reims"). The resulting counter-attack, which started the [Hundred Days Offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hundred_Days_Offensive "Hundred Days Offensive") on 8 August,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERickard2007_209-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTERickard2007-209">[196]</a></sup> led to a marked collapse in German morale.<sup id="cite_ref-210"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-210">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERickard2001_211-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTERickard2001-211">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-212">[199]</a></sup>

#### Allied advance to the Hindenburg Line

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/US23rdInfantry37mmGunInActionFrance1918-ARC531005.gif/220px-US23rdInfantry37mmGunInActionFrance1918-ARC531005.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:US23rdInfantry37mmGunInActionFrance1918-ARC531005.gif)

American soldiers firing on German entrenched positions during the Meuse-Argonne offensive, 1918

By September, the Germans had fallen back to the Hindenburg Line. The Allies had [advanced to the Hindenburg Line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hundred_Days_Offensive#Advance_to_the_Hindenburg_Line "Hundred Days Offensive") in the north and centre. German forces launched numerous counterattacks, but positions and outposts of the Line continued falling, with the BEF alone taking 30,441 prisoners in the last week of September. On 24 September, the Supreme Army Command informed the leaders in Berlin that armistice talks were inevitable.<sup id="cite_ref-Chron-FWW_213-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Chron-FWW-213">[200]</a></sup>

The [final assault](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Offensive "Grand Offensive") on the Hindenburg Line began with the [Meuse-Argonne offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meuse-Argonne_offensive "Meuse-Argonne offensive"), launched by American and French troops on 26 September. Two days later the Allied armies (Belgian, French and British) [attacked around Ypres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fifth_Battle_of_Ypres "Fifth Battle of Ypres"), and the day after the British Fourth and French First Army at St Quentin in the centre of the line. The following week, cooperating American and French units broke through in [Champagne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Champagne_(province) "Champagne (province)") at the [Battle of Blanc Mont Ridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Blanc_Mont_Ridge "Battle of Blanc Mont Ridge") (3–27 October), forcing the Germans off the commanding heights, and closing towards the Belgian frontier.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLellan49_214-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLellan49-214">[201]</a></sup> On 8 October, the Hindenburg Line was pierced by British and Dominion troops of the First and Third British Armies at the [Second Battle of Cambrai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Cambrai_(1918) "Battle of Cambrai (1918)").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristie1997?_215-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristie1997?-215">[202]</a></sup>

#### Breakthrough of Macedonian Front (September 1918)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Bulgarian_major_Ivanov_with_white_flag_surrendering_to_Serbian_7th_Danube_ragiment.jpg/220px-Bulgarian_major_Ivanov_with_white_flag_surrendering_to_Serbian_7th_Danube_ragiment.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bulgarian_major_Ivanov_with_white_flag_surrendering_to_Serbian_7th_Danube_ragiment.jpg)

Bulgarian major Ivanov with white flag surrendering to Serbian 7th Danube regiment near [Kumanovo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kumanovo "Kumanovo")

Allied forces started the [Vardar offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vardar_offensive "Vardar offensive") on 15 September at two key points: [Dobro Pole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dobro_Pole "Dobro Pole") and near [Dojran Lake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dojran_Lake "Dojran Lake"). In the [Battle of Dobro Pole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Dobro_Pole "Battle of Dobro Pole"), the Serbian and French armies had success after a three-day-long battle with relatively small casualties, and subsequently made a breakthrough in the front, something which was rarely seen in World War I. After the front was broken, Allied forces started to liberate Serbia and reached [Skopje](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skopje "Skopje") at 29 September, after which [Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgaria_during_World_War_I "Bulgaria during World War I") signed an armistice with the Allies on 30 September.<sup id="cite_ref-216"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-216">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-217">[204]</a></sup>

### Armistices and capitulations

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Trento_3_novembre_1918.jpg/220px-Trento_3_novembre_1918.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trento_3_novembre_1918.jpg)

Italian troops reach [Trento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trento "Trento") during the [Battle of Vittorio Veneto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Vittorio_Veneto "Battle of Vittorio Veneto"), 1918

The collapse of the Central Powers came swiftly. Bulgaria was the first to sign an armistice, the [Armistice of Salonica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice_of_Salonica "Armistice of Salonica") on 29 September 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-indiana.edu-1918_218-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-indiana.edu-1918-218">[205]</a></sup> German Emperor [Wilhelm II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_II "Wilhelm II") in a telegram to [Bulgarian Tsar Ferdinand I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_Bulgaria "Ferdinand I of Bulgaria") described the situation thus: "Disgraceful! 62,000 Serbs decided the war!".<sup id="cite_ref-219"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-219">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-220">[207]</a></sup> On the same day, the [German Supreme Army Command](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oberste_Heeresleitung "Oberste Heeresleitung") informed Kaiser Wilhelm II and the [Imperial Chancellor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_Chancellor_(Germany) "Imperial Chancellor (Germany)") [Count](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Count "Count") [Georg von Hertling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georg_von_Hertling "Georg von Hertling"), that the military situation facing Germany was hopeless.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAxelrod2018260_221-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAxelrod2018260-221">[208]</a></sup>

On 24 October, the Italians began a push that rapidly recovered territory lost after the Battle of Caporetto. This culminated in the Battle of Vittorio Veneto, marking the end of the Austro-Hungarian Army as an effective fighting force. The offensive also triggered the disintegration of the Austro-Hungarian Empire. During the last week of October, declarations of independence were made in Budapest, Prague, and Zagreb. On 29 October, the imperial authorities asked Italy for an armistice, but the Italians continued advancing, reaching Trento, Udine, and Trieste. On 3 November, Austria-Hungary sent a [flag of truce](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_flag "White flag") to ask for an [armistice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice "Armistice") ([Armistice of Villa Giusti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice_of_Villa_Giusti "Armistice of Villa Giusti")). The terms, arranged with the Allied Authorities in Paris, were communicated to the Austrian commander and accepted. The Armistice with Austria was signed in the Villa Giusti, near [Padua](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Padua "Padua"), on 3 November. Austria and Hungary signed separate armistices following the overthrow of the [Habsburg monarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habsburg_monarchy "Habsburg monarchy"). In the following days, the Italian Army occupied [Innsbruck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Innsbruck "Innsbruck") and all [Tyrol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tyrol "Tyrol"), with over 20,000 soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-222"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-222">[209]</a></sup>

On 30 October, the Ottoman Empire capitulated, and signed the Armistice of Mudros.<sup id="cite_ref-indiana.edu-1918_218-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-indiana.edu-1918-218">[205]</a></sup>

#### German government surrenders

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Armisticetrain.jpg/180px-Armisticetrain.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Armisticetrain.jpg)

[Ferdinand Foch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdinand_Foch "Ferdinand Foch") (_second from right_) pictured outside the [carriage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compi%C3%A8gne_Wagon "Compiègne Wagon") in [Compiègne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compi%C3%A8gne "Compiègne") after agreeing to the [armistice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice_of_11_November_1918 "Armistice of 11 November 1918") that ended the war there.<sup id="cite_ref-223"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-223">[210]</a></sup>

With the military faltering and with widespread loss of confidence in the Kaiser leading to his abdication and fleeing of the country, Germany moved towards surrender. Prince Maximilian of Baden took charge of a new government on October 3 as Chancellor of Germany to negotiate with the Allies. Negotiations with President Wilson began immediately, in the hope that he would offer better terms than the British and French. Wilson demanded a constitutional monarchy and parliamentary control over the German military.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStevenson2004385_224-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStevenson2004385-224">[211]</a></sup>

In northern Germany, the [German Revolution of 1918–1919](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Revolution_of_1918%E2%80%931919 "German Revolution of 1918–1919") began at the end of October 1918. Units of the German Navy refused to set sail for a last, large-scale operation in a war they believed to be as good as lost, initiating the uprising. The [sailors' revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiel_mutiny "Kiel mutiny"), which then ensued in the naval ports of [Wilhelmshaven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelmshaven "Wilhelmshaven") and [Kiel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiel "Kiel"), spread across the whole country within days and led to the [proclamation of a republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_republic_in_Germany "Proclamation of the republic in Germany") on 9 November 1918, shortly thereafter to the [abdication of Kaiser Wilhelm II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdication_of_Wilhelm_II "Abdication of Wilhelm II"), and German surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-225"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-225">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-226">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-227">[214]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStevenson2004383_228-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStevenson2004383-228">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStevenson2004Chapter_17_229-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStevenson2004Chapter_17-229">[216]</a></sup>

## Aftermath

In the aftermath of the war, four empires disappeared: the German, Austro-Hungarian, Ottoman, and Russian.<sup id="cite_ref-230"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-230">[n]</a></sup> Numerous nations regained their former independence, and new ones were created. Four dynasties fell as a result of the war: the [Romanovs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Romanov "House of Romanov"), the [Hohenzollerns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Hohenzollern "House of Hohenzollern"), the [Habsburgs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Habsburg "House of Habsburg"), and the [Ottomans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_dynasty "Ottoman dynasty"). Belgium and Serbia were badly damaged, as was France, with 1.4 million soldiers dead,<sup id="cite_ref-231"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-231">[217]</a></sup> not counting other casualties. Germany and Russia were similarly affected.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker_2005_2732_232-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Tucker_2005_2732-232">[218]</a></sup>

### Formal end of the war

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/William_Orpen_-_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors.jpg/180px-William_Orpen_-_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:William_Orpen_-_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors.jpg)

The signing of the [Treaty of Versailles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles "Treaty of Versailles") in the [Hall of Mirrors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hall_of_Mirrors "Hall of Mirrors"), Versailles, 28 June 1919, by Sir [William Orpen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Orpen "William Orpen")

A formal state of war between the two sides persisted for another seven months, until the signing of the [Treaty of Versailles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles "Treaty of Versailles") with Germany on 28 June 1919. The United States Senate did not ratify the treaty despite public support for it,<sup id="cite_ref-233"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-233">[219]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-234">[220]</a></sup> and did not formally end its involvement in the war until the [Knox–Porter Resolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knox%E2%80%93Porter_Resolution "Knox–Porter Resolution") was signed on 2 July 1921 by President [Warren G. Harding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warren_G._Harding "Warren G. Harding").<sup id="cite_ref-235"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-235">[221]</a></sup> For the British Empire, the state of war ceased under the provisions of the _[Termination of the Present War (Definition) Act 1918](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Termination_of_the_Present_War_(Definition)_Act_1918 "Termination of the Present War (Definition) Act 1918")_ concerning:

-   Germany on 10 January 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-236"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-236">[222]</a></sup>
-   Austria on 16 July 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-237"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-237">[223]</a></sup>
-   Bulgaria on 9 August 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-238"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-238">[224]</a></sup>
-   Hungary on 26 July 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-239"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-239">[225]</a></sup>
-   Turkey on 6 August 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-240"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-240">[226]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Venizelos_signing_the_Treaty_of_Sevres.jpeg/220px-Venizelos_signing_the_Treaty_of_Sevres.jpeg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Venizelos_signing_the_Treaty_of_Sevres.jpeg)

Greek prime minister [Eleftherios Venizelos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eleftherios_Venizelos "Eleftherios Venizelos") signing the [Treaty of Sèvres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres "Treaty of Sèvres")

Some [war memorials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_memorial "War memorial") date the end of the war as being when the Versailles Treaty was signed in 1919, which was when many of the troops serving abroad finally returned home; by contrast, most commemorations of the war's end concentrate on the armistice of 11 November 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-241"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-241">[227]</a></sup>

### Peace treaties and national boundaries

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Map_Europe_1923-en.svg/280px-Map_Europe_1923-en.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Map_Europe_1923-en.svg)

Map of [territorial changes in Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_national_border_changes_(1914%E2%80%93present) "List of national border changes (1914–present)") after World War I (as of 1923)

After the war, there grew a certain amount of academic focus on the causes of war and on the elements that could make peace flourish. In part, these led to the institutionalization of peace and conflict studies, security studies and International Relations (IR) in general.<sup id="cite_ref-242"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-242">[228]</a></sup> The [Paris Peace Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference_(1919%E2%80%931920) "Paris Peace Conference (1919–1920)") imposed a series of peace treaties on the Central Powers officially ending the war. The 1919 [Treaty of Versailles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles "Treaty of Versailles") dealt with Germany and, building on [Wilson's 14th point](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourteen_Points "Fourteen Points"), established the [League of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_Nations "League of Nations") on 28 June 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMagliveras19998–12_243-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMagliveras19998%E2%80%9312-243">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorthedge198635–36_244-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorthedge198635%E2%80%9336-244">[230]</a></sup>

The Central Powers had to acknowledge responsibility for "all the loss and damage to which the Allied and Associated Governments and their nationals have been subjected as a consequence of the war imposed upon them by" their aggression. In the Treaty of Versailles, this statement was [Article 231](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Article_231_of_the_Treaty_of_Versailles "Article 231 of the Treaty of Versailles"). This article became known as the "War Guilt Clause", as the majority of Germans felt humiliated and resentful.<sup id="cite_ref-245"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-245">[231]</a></sup> Overall, the Germans felt they had been unjustly dealt with by what they called the "[diktat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diktat "Diktat") of Versailles". German historian Hagen Schulze said the Treaty placed Germany "under legal sanctions, deprived of military power, economically ruined, and politically humiliated."<sup id="cite_ref-246"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-246">[232]</a></sup> Belgian historian Laurence Van Ypersele emphasises the central role played by memory of the war and the Versailles Treaty in German politics in the 1920s and 1930s:

> Active denial of war guilt in Germany and German resentment at both reparations and continued Allied occupation of the Rhineland made widespread revision of the meaning and memory of the war problematic. The legend of the "[stab in the back](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stab-in-the-back_myth "Stab-in-the-back myth")" and the wish to revise the "Versailles diktat", and the belief in an international threat aimed at the elimination of the German nation persisted at the heart of German politics. Even a man of peace such as \[[Gustav](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gustav_Stresemann "Gustav Stresemann")\] Stresemann publicly rejected German guilt. As for the Nazis, they waved the banners of domestic treason and international conspiracy in an attempt to galvanise the German nation into a spirit of revenge. Like a Fascist Italy, Nazi Germany sought to redirect the memory of the war to the benefit of its policies.<sup id="cite_ref-247"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-247">[233]</a></sup>

Meanwhile, new nations liberated from German rule viewed the treaty as a recognition of wrongs committed against small nations by much larger aggressive neighbours.<sup id="cite_ref-248"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-248">[234]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary.png/280px-Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary.png)

[Dissolution of Austria-Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary "Dissolution of Austria-Hungary") after war

Austria-Hungary was partitioned into several successor states, largely but not entirely along ethnic lines. Apart from Austria and Hungary, Czechoslovakia, Italy, Poland, Romania and Yugoslavia received territories from the Dual Monarchy (the formerly separate and autonomous [Kingdom of Croatia-Slavonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Croatia-Slavonia "Kingdom of Croatia-Slavonia") was incorporated into Yugoslavia). The details were contained in the treaties of [Saint-Germain-en-Laye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Saint-Germain-en-Laye_(1919) "Treaty of Saint-Germain-en-Laye (1919)") and [Trianon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon "Treaty of Trianon"). As a result, Hungary lost 64% of its total population, decreasing from 20.9 million to 7.6 million, and losing 31% (3.3 out of 10.7 million) of its ethnic [Hungarians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_people "Hungarian people").<sup id="cite_ref-249"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-249">[235]</a></sup> According to the 1910 census, speakers of the Hungarian language included approximately 54% of the entire population of the [Kingdom of Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary "Kingdom of Hungary").
