Within the country, numerous ethnic minorities were present: 16.1% [Romanians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanians "Romanians"), 10.5% [Slovaks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slovaks "Slovaks"), 10.4% [Germans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germans "Germans"), 2.5% [Ruthenians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruthenians "Ruthenians"), 2.5% [Serbs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbs "Serbs") and 8% others.<sup id="cite_ref-Frucht,_p._356_250-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Frucht,_p._356-250">[236]</a></sup> Between 1920 and 1924, 354,000 Hungarians fled former Hungarian territories attached to Romania, Czechoslovakia, and Yugoslavia.<sup id="cite_ref-251"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-251">[237]</a></sup>

The Russian Empire, which withdrew from the war in 1917 after the October Revolution, lost much of its western frontier as the newly independent nations of [Estonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Estonia#Road_to_the_republic "History of Estonia"), [Finland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Finland#Independence_and_Civil_War "History of Finland"), [Latvia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Latvia#Independence "History of Latvia"), [Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Lithuania#Independent_Lithuania_(1918%E2%80%9340) "History of Lithuania"), and [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic "Second Polish Republic") were carved from it. Romania took control of Bessarabia in April 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClark1927_252-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark1927-252">[238]</a></sup>

### National identities

After 123 years, Poland re-emerged as an independent country. The Kingdom of Serbia and its dynasty, as a "minor Entente nation" and the country with the most casualties per capita,<sup id="cite_ref-253"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-253">[239]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-254">[240]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-255">[241]</a></sup> became the backbone of a new multinational state, the [Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia "Kingdom of Yugoslavia"), later renamed Yugoslavia. Czechoslovakia, combining the [Kingdom of Bohemia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bohemia "Kingdom of Bohemia") with parts of the Kingdom of Hungary, became a new nation. Romania would [unite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Union "Great Union") all Romanian-speaking people under a single state, leading to [Greater Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Romania "Greater Romania").<sup id="cite_ref-256"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-256">[242]</a></sup>

In Australia and New Zealand, the Battle of Gallipoli became known as those nations' "Baptism of Fire". It was the first major war in which the newly established countries fought, and it was one of the first times that Australian troops fought as Australians, not just subjects of the [British Crown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Crown "The Crown"), and independent national identities for these nations took hold. [Anzac Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anzac_Day "Anzac Day"), commemorating the Australian and New Zealand Army Corps (ANZAC), celebrates this defining moment.<sup id="cite_ref-257"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-257">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-awmtradition_258-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-awmtradition-258">[244]</a></sup>

In the aftermath of World War I, Greece [fought](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Turkish_War_(1919%E2%80%931922) "Greco-Turkish War (1919–1922)") against Turkish nationalists led by [Mustafa Kemal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk "Mustafa Kemal Atatürk"), a war that eventually resulted in a [massive population exchange between the two countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_exchange_between_Greece_and_Turkey "Population exchange between Greece and Turkey") under the Treaty of Lausanne.<sup id="cite_ref-259"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-259">[245]</a></sup> According to various sources,<sup id="cite_ref-260"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-260">[246]</a></sup> several hundred thousand Greeks died during this period, which was tied in with the Greek genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-261"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-261">[247]</a></sup>

## Casualties

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Transporting_Ottoman_injured_at_Sirkedji.jpg/220px-Transporting_Ottoman_injured_at_Sirkedji.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Transporting_Ottoman_injured_at_Sirkedji.jpg)

Transporting Ottoman wounded at [Sirkeci](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sirkeci "Sirkeci")

Of the 60 million European military personnel who were mobilised from 1914 to 1918, an estimated [8 million were killed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I_casualties "World War I casualties"), 7 million were permanently disabled, and 15 million were seriously injured. Germany lost 15.1% of its active male population, Austria-Hungary lost 17.1%, and France lost 10.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKitchen200022_262-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKitchen200022-262">[248]</a></sup> France mobilised 7.8 million men, of which 1.4 million died and 3.2 million were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-263"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-263">[249]</a></sup> Approximately 15,000 sustained horrific facial injuries, causing social stigma and marginalisation; they were called the _[gueules cassées](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gueules_cass%C3%A9es "Gueules cassées")_. In Germany, civilian deaths were 474,000 higher than in peacetime, due in large part to food shortages and malnutrition that had weakened disease resistance. These excess deaths are estimated as 271,000 in 1918, plus another 71,000 in the first half of 1919 when the blockade was still in effect.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoward1993166_264-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward1993166-264">[250]</a></sup> Starvation caused by famine killed approximately 100,000 people in Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESaadi2009_265-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTESaadi2009-265">[251]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Emergency_hospital_during_Influenza_epidemic%2C_Camp_Funston%2C_Kansas_-_NCP_1603.jpg/220px-Emergency_hospital_during_Influenza_epidemic%2C_Camp_Funston%2C_Kansas_-_NCP_1603.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Emergency_hospital_during_Influenza_epidemic,_Camp_Funston,_Kansas_-_NCP_1603.jpg)

Emergency military hospital during the [Spanish flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_flu "Spanish flu") pandemic in [Camp Funston](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_Funston "Camp Funston"), [Kansas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kansas "Kansas"), 1918

Diseases flourished in the chaotic wartime conditions. In 1914 alone, louse-borne [epidemic typhus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epidemic_typhus "Epidemic typhus") killed 200,000 in Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETschanz_266-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETschanz-266">[252]</a></sup> Starting in early 1918, a major influenza epidemic known as [Spanish flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_flu "Spanish flu") spread around the world, accelerated by the movement of large numbers of soldiers, often crammed together in camps and transport ships with poor sanitation. The Spanish flu killed at least 17 million to 25 million people,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpreeuwenberg20182561–2567_267-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpreeuwenberg20182561%E2%80%932567-267">[253]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKnoblerMackMahmoudLemon2005_268-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKnoblerMackMahmoudLemon2005-268">[254]</a></sup> including an estimated 2.64 million Europeans and as many as 675,000 Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-Ansart_et_al._2009_269-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Ansart_et_al._2009-269">[255]</a></sup> Between 1915 and 1926, an epidemic of [encephalitis lethargica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Encephalitis_lethargica "Encephalitis lethargica") spread around the world affecting nearly five million people.<sup id="cite_ref-270"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-270">[256]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reid_2001_271-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Reid_2001-271">[257]</a></sup>

8 million [equines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equus_(genus) "Equus (genus)") including [horses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horse "Horse"), [donkeys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donkey "Donkey") and [mules](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mule "Mule") died, three-quarters of them from the extreme conditions they worked in.<sup id="cite_ref-272"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-272">[258]</a></sup>

### War crimes

#### Chemical weapons in warfare

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/French_soldiers_making_a_gas_and_flame_attack_on_German_trenches_in_Flanders._Belgium.%2C_ca._1900_-_1982_-_NARA_-_530722.tif/lossy-page1-220px-French_soldiers_making_a_gas_and_flame_attack_on_German_trenches_in_Flanders._Belgium.%2C_ca._1900_-_1982_-_NARA_-_530722.tif.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:French_soldiers_making_a_gas_and_flame_attack_on_German_trenches_in_Flanders._Belgium.,_ca._1900_-_1982_-_NARA_-_530722.tif)

French soldiers making a gas and flame attack on German trenches in Flanders

The German army was the first to successfully deploy chemical weapons during the Second Battle of Ypres (22 April – 25 May 1915), after German scientists working under the direction of [Fritz Haber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fritz_Haber "Fritz Haber") at the [Kaiser Wilhelm Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaiser_Wilhelm_Society "Kaiser Wilhelm Society") developed a method to weaponize [chlorine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorine "Chlorine").<sup id="cite_ref-274"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-274">[o]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AJPH_275-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-AJPH-275">[260]</a></sup> The use of chemical weapons had been sanctioned by the German High Command to force Allied soldiers out of their entrenched positions, complementing rather than supplanting more lethal conventional weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-AJPH_275-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-AJPH-275">[260]</a></sup> In time, chemical weapons were deployed by all major belligerents throughout the war, inflicting approximately 1.3 million casualties, of which about 90,000 were fatal.<sup id="cite_ref-AJPH_275-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-AJPH-275">[260]</a></sup> For example, there were an estimated 186,000 British chemical weapons casualties during the war (80% of which were the result of exposure to the [vesicant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blister_agent "Blister agent") '[mustard gas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustard_gas "Mustard gas")', introduced to the battlefield by the Germans in July 1917),<sup id="cite_ref-AJPH_275-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-AJPH-275">[260]</a></sup> and up to one-third of American casualties were caused by them. The Russian Army reportedly suffered roughly 500,000 chemical weapon casualties in World War I.<sup id="cite_ref-276"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-276">[261]</a></sup> The use of chemical weapons in warfare was a direct violation of the [1899 Hague Declaration Concerning Asphyxiating Gases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hague_Conventions_of_1899_and_1907#Hague_Convention_of_1899 "Hague Conventions of 1899 and 1907") and the [1907 Hague Convention on Land Warfare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hague_Conventions_of_1899_and_1907 "Hague Conventions of 1899 and 1907"), which prohibited their use.<sup id="cite_ref-277"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-277">[262]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-278">[263]</a></sup>

#### Genocides by the Ottoman Empire

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Ambassador_Morgenthau%27s_Story_p314.jpg/220px-Ambassador_Morgenthau%27s_Story_p314.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ambassador_Morgenthau%27s_Story_p314.jpg)

Armenians killed during the Armenian genocide. Image taken from _Ambassador Morgenthau's Story_, written by [Henry Morgenthau Sr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Morgenthau_Sr. "Henry Morgenthau Sr.") and published in 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-279"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-279">[264]</a></sup>

The [ethnic cleansing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing "Ethnic cleansing") of the Ottoman Empire's Armenian population, including mass deportations and executions, during the final years of the Ottoman Empire is considered [genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genocide "Genocide").<sup id="cite_ref-IAGSletter_280-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-IAGSletter-280">[265]</a></sup> The Ottomans carried out organised and systematic massacres of the Armenian population at the beginning of the war and manipulated acts of Armenian resistance by portraying them as rebellions to justify further extermination.<sup id="cite_ref-leverkun_281-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-leverkun-281">[266]</a></sup> In early 1915, several Armenians volunteered to join the Russian forces and the Ottoman government used this as a pretext to issue the [Tehcir Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temporary_Law_of_Deportation "Temporary Law of Deportation") (Law on Deportation), which authorised the deportation of Armenians from the Empire's eastern provinces to Syria between 1915 and 1918. The Armenians were intentionally [marched to death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_march "Death march") and a number were attacked by Ottoman brigands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2006177_282-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2006177-282">[267]</a></sup> While an exact number of deaths is unknown, the [International Association of Genocide Scholars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Association_of_Genocide_Scholars "International Association of Genocide Scholars") estimates 1.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-IAGSletter_280-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-IAGSletter-280">[265]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-283"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-283">[268]</a></sup> The government of Turkey continues to [deny the genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide_denial "Armenian genocide denial") to the present day, arguing that those who died were victims of inter-ethnic fighting, famine, or disease during World War I; these claims are rejected by most historians.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFromkin1989212–215_284-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFromkin1989212%E2%80%93215-284">[269]</a></sup>

Other ethnic groups were similarly attacked by the Ottoman Empire during this period, including Assyrians and [Greeks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_genocide "Greek genocide"), and some scholars consider those events to be part of the same policy of extermination.<sup id="cite_ref-285"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-285">[270]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-286">[271]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-287">[272]</a></sup> At least 250,000 Assyrian Christians, about half of the population, and 350,000–750,000 [Anatolian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greeks_in_Turkey "Greeks in Turkey") and [Pontic Greeks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pontic_Greeks "Pontic Greeks") were killed between 1915 and 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-288"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-288">[273]</a></sup>

### Prisoners of war

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/1stGazaBritishPrisoners00118v.jpg/220px-1stGazaBritishPrisoners00118v.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1stGazaBritishPrisoners00118v.jpg)

British prisoners guarded by Ottoman forces after the [First Battle of Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Battle_of_Gaza "First Battle of Gaza") in 1917

About eight million soldiers surrendered and were held in [POW camps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoner-of-war_camp "Prisoner-of-war camp") during the war. All nations pledged to follow the [Hague Conventions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hague_Conventions_of_1899_and_1907 "Hague Conventions of 1899 and 1907") on fair treatment of [prisoners of war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoner_of_war "Prisoner of war"), and the survival rate for POWs was generally much higher than that of combatants at the front.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhillimoreBellot19194–64_289-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhillimoreBellot19194%E2%80%9364-289">[274]</a></sup>

25–31% of Russian losses (as a proportion of those captured, wounded, or killed) were to prisoner status; for Austria-Hungary 32%; for Italy 26%; for France 12%; for Germany 9%; for Britain 7%. Prisoners from the Allied armies totalled about 1.4 million (not including Russia, which lost 2.5–3.5 million soldiers as prisoners). From the Central Powers, about 3.3 million soldiers became prisoners; most of them surrendered to Russians.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson1999368–369_290-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson1999368%E2%80%93369-290">[275]</a></sup>

## Soldiers' experiences

Allied personnel was around 42,928,000, while Central personnel was near 25,248,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker_2005_2732_232-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Tucker_2005_2732-232">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts20052733_291-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts20052733-291">[276]</a></sup> The British soldiers of the war were initially volunteers but increasingly were [conscripted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscription "Conscription"). Surviving veterans, returning home, often found they could discuss their experiences only among themselves. Grouping, they formed "veterans' associations" or "Legions". A small number of personal accounts of American veterans have been collected by the Library of Congress [Veterans History Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veterans_History_Project "Veterans History Project").<sup id="cite_ref-292"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-292">[277]</a></sup>

### Conscription

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/I_want_you_for_U.S._Army_3b48465u_edit.jpg/220px-I_want_you_for_U.S._Army_3b48465u_edit.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:I_want_you_for_U.S._Army_3b48465u_edit.jpg)

U.S. Army recruiting poster with [Uncle Sam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uncle_Sam "Uncle Sam")

Conscription was common in most European countries. However, it was controversial in English-speaking countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHavighurst1985131_293-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHavighurst1985131-293">[278]</a></sup> It was especially unpopular among minority ethnicities—especially the Irish Catholics in Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-294"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-294">[279]</a></sup> Australia,<sup id="cite_ref-295"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-295">[280]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-parl_296-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-parl-296">[281]</a></sup> and the French Catholics in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-297"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-297">[282]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-298">[283]</a></sup>

In the United States, conscription began in 1917 and was generally well-received, with a few pockets of opposition in isolated rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-299"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-299">[284]</a></sup> The administration decided to rely primarily on conscription, rather than voluntary enlistment, to raise military manpower after only 73,000 volunteers enlisted out of the initial 1 million target in the first six weeks of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-300"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-300">[285]</a></sup>

### Military attachés and war correspondents

Military and civilian observers from every major power closely followed the course of the war. Many were able to report on events from a perspective somewhat akin to modern "[embedded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embedded_journalism "Embedded journalism")" positions within the opposing land and naval forces.

## Economic effects

Macro- and micro-economic consequences devolved from the war. Families were altered by the departure of many men. With the death or absence of the primary wage earner, women were forced into the workforce in unprecedented numbers. At the same time, the industry needed to replace the lost labourers sent to war. This aided the struggle for [voting rights for women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suffragette "Suffragette").<sup id="cite_ref-301"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-301">[286]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/The_Girl_Behind_the_Gun_1915.jpg/220px-The_Girl_Behind_the_Gun_1915.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Girl_Behind_the_Gun_1915.jpg)

Poster showing women workers, 1915

In all nations, the government's share of GDP increased, surpassing 50% in both Germany and France and nearly reaching that level in Britain. To pay for purchases in the United States, Britain cashed in its extensive investments in American railroads and then began borrowing heavily from [Wall Street](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wall_Street "Wall Street"). President Wilson was on the verge of cutting off the loans in late 1916 but allowed a great increase in [US government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States "Federal government of the United States") lending to the Allies. After 1919, the US demanded repayment of these loans. The repayments were, in part, funded by German reparations that, in turn, were supported by American loans to Germany. This circular system collapsed in 1931 and some loans were never repaid. Britain still owed the United States $4.4 [billion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1,000,000,000 "1,000,000,000")<sup id="cite_ref-302"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-302">[p]</a></sup> of World War I debt in 1934; the last installment was finally paid in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-303"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-303">[287]</a></sup>

Britain turned to her colonies for help in obtaining essential war materials whose supply from traditional sources had become difficult. Geologists such as [Albert Kitson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Kitson "Albert Kitson") were called on to find new resources of precious minerals in the African colonies. Kitson discovered important new deposits of [manganese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manganese "Manganese"), used in munitions production, in the [Gold Coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gold_Coast_(region) "Gold Coast (region)").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreen1938cxxvi_304-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreen1938cxxvi-304">[288]</a></sup>

Article 231 of the Treaty of Versailles (the so-called "war guilt" clause) stated Germany accepted responsibility for "all the loss and damage to which the Allied and Associated Governments and their nationals have been subjected as a consequence of the war imposed upon them by the aggression of Germany and her allies."<sup id="cite_ref-305"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-305">[289]</a></sup> It was worded as such to lay a legal basis for reparations, and a similar clause was inserted in the treaties with Austria and Hungary. However, neither of them interpreted it as an admission of war guilt.<sup id="cite_ref-306"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-306">[290]</a></sup> In 1921, the total reparation sum was placed at 132 billion gold marks. However, "Allied experts knew that Germany could not pay" this sum. The total sum was divided into three categories, with the third being "deliberately designed to be chimerical" and its "primary function was to mislead public opinion ... into believing the 'total sum was being maintained.'"<sup id="cite_ref-Marks237_307-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Marks237-307">[291]</a></sup> Thus, 50 billion gold marks (12.5 billion dollars) "represented the actual Allied assessment of German capacity to pay" and "therefore … represented the total German reparations" figure that had to be paid.<sup id="cite_ref-Marks237_307-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Marks237-307">[291]</a></sup>

This figure could be paid in cash or in-kind (coal, timber, chemical dyes, etc.). In addition, some of the territory lost—via the Treaty of Versailles—was credited towards the reparation figure as were other acts such as helping to restore the Library of Louvain.<sup id="cite_ref-308"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-308">[292]</a></sup> By 1929, the [Great Depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression "Great Depression") arrived, causing political chaos throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-309"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-309">[293]</a></sup> In 1932 the payment of reparations was suspended by the international community, by which point Germany had paid only the equivalent of 20.598 billion gold marks in reparations.<sup id="cite_ref-310"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-310">[294]</a></sup> With the rise of Adolf Hitler, all bonds and loans that had been issued and taken out during the 1920s and early 1930s were cancelled. [David Andelman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_A._Andelman "David A. Andelman") notes "Refusing to pay doesn't make an agreement null and void. The bonds, the agreement, still exist." Thus, following the Second World War, at the [London Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_Agreement_on_German_External_Debts "London Agreement on German External Debts") in 1953, Germany agreed to resume payment on the money borrowed. On 3 October 2010, Germany made the final payment on these bonds.<sup id="cite_ref-315"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-315">[q]</a></sup>

The Australian prime minister, [Billy Hughes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billy_Hughes "Billy Hughes"), wrote to the British prime minister, [David Lloyd George](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Lloyd_George "David Lloyd George"), "You have assured us that you cannot get better terms. I much regret it, and hope even now that some way may be found of securing agreement for demanding reparation commensurate with the tremendous sacrifices made by the British Empire and her Allies." Australia received £5,571,720 in war reparations, but the direct cost of the war to Australia had been £376,993,052, and, by the mid-1930s, repatriation pensions, war gratuities, interest and sinking fund charges were £831,280,947.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouter2000354_316-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouter2000354-316">[299]</a></sup> Of about 416,000 Australians who served, about 60,000 were killed and another 152,000 were wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker_2005_2732_232-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Tucker_2005_2732-232">[218]</a></sup>

The war contributed to the evolution of the [wristwatch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Watch "Watch") from women's jewellery to a practical everyday item, replacing the [pocketwatch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pocket_watch "Pocket watch"), which requires a free hand to operate.<sup id="cite_ref-npr_317-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-npr-317">[300]</a></sup> [Trench watches](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trench_watch "Trench watch") were designed for use by the military as pocket watches were not as effective for combat. Military funding of advancements in radio contributed to the post-war popularity of the medium.<sup id="cite_ref-npr_317-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-npr-317">[300]</a></sup>

## Support and opposition for the war

### Support

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Affiche-guerre_Femmes-au-travail.jpg/180px-Affiche-guerre_Femmes-au-travail.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Affiche-guerre_Femmes-au-travail.jpg)

Poster urging women to join the British war effort, published by the [Young Women's Christian Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YWCA "YWCA")

In the Balkans, [Yugoslav nationalists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yugoslavism "Yugoslavism") such as the leader, [Ante Trumbić](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ante_Trumbi%C4%87 "Ante Trumbić"), strongly supported the war, desiring the freedom of [Yugoslavs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yugoslavs "Yugoslavs") from Austria-Hungary and other foreign powers and the creation of an independent Yugoslavia. The [Yugoslav Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yugoslav_Committee "Yugoslav Committee"), led by Trumbić, was formed in Paris on 30 April 1915 but shortly moved its office to London.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts20051189_318-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts20051189-318">[301]</a></sup> In April 1918, the Rome Congress of Oppressed Nationalities met, including [Czechoslovak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovakism "Czechoslovakism"), Italian, [Polish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_people "Polish people"), [Transylvanian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transylvania "Transylvania"), and Yugoslav representatives who urged the Allies to support national [self-determination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-determination "Self-determination") for the peoples residing within Austria-Hungary.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_319-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-autogenerated3-319">[302]</a></sup>

In the Middle East, [Arab nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_nationalism "Arab nationalism") soared in Ottoman territories in response to the rise of Turkish nationalism during the war, with Arab nationalist leaders advocating the creation of a [pan-Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan-Arabism "Pan-Arabism") state. In 1916, the Arab Revolt began in Ottoman-controlled territories of the Middle East to achieve independence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005117_320-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005117-320">[303]</a></sup>

In East Africa, [Iyasu V](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lij_Iyasu_of_Ethiopia "Lij Iyasu of Ethiopia") of [Ethiopia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire "Ethiopian Empire") was supporting the [Dervish state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dervish_movement_(Somali) "Dervish movement (Somali)") who were at war with the British in the [Somaliland campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Somaliland_campaign "Somaliland campaign").<sup id="cite_ref-321"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-321">[304]</a></sup> Von Syburg, the German envoy in [Addis Ababa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Addis_Ababa "Addis Ababa"), said, "now the time has come for Ethiopia to regain the coast of the Red Sea driving the Italians home, to restore the Empire to its ancient size." The Ethiopian Empire was on the verge of entering World War I on the side of the Central Powers before Iyasu's overthrow at the [Battle of Segale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Segale "Battle of Segale") due to Allied pressure on the Ethiopian aristocracy.<sup id="cite_ref-322"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-322">[305]</a></sup> Iyasu was accused of converting to [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam").<sup id="cite_ref-323"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-323">[306]</a></sup> According to Ethiopian historian [Bahru Zewde](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bahru_Zewde "Bahru Zewde"), the evidence used to prove Iyasu's conversion was a doctored photo of Iyasu wearing a turban provided by the Allies.<sup id="cite_ref-324"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-324">[307]</a></sup> Some historians claim the British spy [T. E. Lawrence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T._E._Lawrence "T. E. Lawrence") forged the photo.<sup id="cite_ref-325"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-325">[308]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/BVRC-Great-War-Contingent_1914.jpg/220px-BVRC-Great-War-Contingent_1914.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:BVRC-Great-War-Contingent_1914.jpg)

[Bermuda Volunteer Rifle Corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bermuda_Volunteer_Rifle_Corps "Bermuda Volunteer Rifle Corps") First Contingent in Bermuda, winter 1914–1915, before joining [1 Lincolnshire Regiment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Lincolnshire_Regiment "Royal Lincolnshire Regiment") in France in June 1915. The dozen remaining after [Guedecourt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capture_of_Gueudecourt "Capture of Gueudecourt") on 25 September 1916, merged with a Second Contingent. The two contingents suffered 75% casualties.

Several socialist parties initially supported the war when it began in August 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_319-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-autogenerated3-319">[302]</a></sup> But European socialists split on national lines, with the concept of [class conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_conflict "Class conflict") held by radical socialists such as Marxists and [syndicalists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syndicalism "Syndicalism") being overborne by their patriotic support for the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts20051069_326-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts20051069-326">[309]</a></sup> Once the war began, Austrian, British, French, German, and Russian socialists followed the rising nationalist current by supporting their countries' intervention in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005884_327-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005884-327">[310]</a></sup>

[Italian nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_nationalism "Italian nationalism") was stirred by the outbreak of the war and was initially strongly supported by a variety of political factions. One of the most prominent and popular Italian nationalist supporters of the war was [Gabriele D'Annunzio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabriele_D%27Annunzio "Gabriele D'Annunzio"), who promoted [Italian irredentism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_irredentism "Italian irredentism") and helped sway the Italian public to support intervention in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005335_328-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005335-328">[311]</a></sup> The [Italian Liberal Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Liberal_Party "Italian Liberal Party"), under the leadership of [Paolo Boselli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paolo_Boselli "Paolo Boselli"), promoted intervention in the war on the side of the Allies and used the Dante Alighieri Society to promote Italian nationalism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005219_329-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005219-329">[312]</a></sup> Italian socialists were divided on whether to support the war or oppose it; some were militant supporters of the war, including [Benito Mussolini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benito_Mussolini "Benito Mussolini") and [Leonida Bissolati](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonida_Bissolati "Leonida Bissolati").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005209_330-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005209-330">[313]</a></sup> However, the [Italian Socialist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Socialist_Party "Italian Socialist Party") decided to oppose the war after anti-militarist protestors were killed, resulting in a [general strike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_strike "General strike") called [Red Week](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Week_(Italy) "Red Week (Italy)").<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_331-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-autogenerated6-331">[314]</a></sup> The Italian Socialist Party purged itself of pro-war nationalist members, including Mussolini.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_331-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-autogenerated6-331">[314]</a></sup> Mussolini, a syndicalist who supported the war on grounds of irredentist claims on Italian-populated regions of Austria-Hungary, formed the pro-interventionist _[Il Popolo d'Italia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Il_Popolo_d%27Italia "Il Popolo d'Italia")_ and the _Fasci Rivoluzionario d'Azione Internazionalista_ ("Revolutionary [Fasci](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascio "Fascio") for International Action") in October 1914 that later developed into the _[Fasci Italiani di Combattimento](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fasci_Italiani_di_Combattimento "Fasci Italiani di Combattimento")_ in 1919, the origin of fascism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005826_332-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005826-332">[315]</a></sup> Mussolini's nationalism enabled him to raise funds from [Ansaldo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gio._Ansaldo_%26_C. "Gio. Ansaldo & C.") (an armaments firm) and other companies to create _Il Popolo d'Italia_ to convince socialists and revolutionaries to support the war.<sup id="cite_ref-333"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-333">[316]</a></sup>

#### Patriotic funds

On both sides, there was large-scale fundraising for soldiers' welfare, their dependents and those injured. The [Nail Men](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nail_Men "Nail Men") were a German example. Around the British Empire, there were many patriotic funds, including the [Royal Patriotic Fund Corporation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Patriotic_Fund_Corporation "Royal Patriotic Fund Corporation"), [Canadian Patriotic Fund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canadian_Patriotic_Fund "Canadian Patriotic Fund"), [Queensland Patriotic Fund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queensland_Patriotic_Fund "Queensland Patriotic Fund") and, by 1919, there were 983 funds in New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-334"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-334">[317]</a></sup> At the start of the next world war the New Zealand funds were reformed, having been criticised as overlapping, wasteful and abused,<sup id="cite_ref-335"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-335">[318]</a></sup> but 11 were still functioning in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-336"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-336">[319]</a></sup>

### Opposition

Many countries jailed those who spoke out against the conflict. These included [Eugene Debs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugene_V._Debs "Eugene V. Debs") in the United States and [Bertrand Russell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bertrand_Russell "Bertrand Russell") in Britain. In the US, the [Espionage Act of 1917](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Espionage_Act_of_1917 "Espionage Act of 1917") and [Sedition Act of 1918](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedition_Act_of_1918 "Sedition Act of 1918") made it a federal crime to oppose military recruitment or make any statements deemed "disloyal". Publications at all critical of the government were removed from circulation by postal censors,<sup id="cite_ref-Karp-PoW-1979_337-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Karp-PoW-1979-337">[320]</a></sup> and many served long prison sentences for statements of fact deemed unpatriotic.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Sackville_Street_%28Dublin%29_after_the_1916_Easter_Rising.JPG/220px-Sackville_Street_%28Dublin%29_after_the_1916_Easter_Rising.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sackville_Street_(Dublin)_after_the_1916_Easter_Rising.JPG)

Sackville Street (now [O'Connell Street](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/O%27Connell_Street "O'Connell Street")) after the 1916 [Easter Rising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Easter_Rising "Easter Rising") in Dublin

Several nationalists opposed intervention, particularly within states that the nationalists were hostile to. Although the vast majority of Irish people consented to participate in the war in 1914 and 1915, a minority of advanced [Irish nationalists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irish_nationalism "Irish nationalism") had staunchly opposed taking part.<sup id="cite_ref-338"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-338">[321]</a></sup> The war began amid the Home Rule crisis in Ireland that had resurfaced in 1912, and by July 1914 there was a serious possibility of an outbreak of civil war in Ireland. Irish nationalists and Marxists attempted to pursue Irish independence, culminating in the [Easter Rising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Easter_Rising "Easter Rising") of 1916, with Germany sending 20,000 rifles to Ireland to stir unrest in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005584_339-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerRoberts2005584-339">[322]</a></sup> The UK government placed Ireland under [martial law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martial_law "Martial law") in response to the Easter Rising, though once the immediate threat of revolution had dissipated, the authorities did try to make concessions to nationalist feeling.<sup id="cite_ref-340"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-340">[323]</a></sup> However, opposition to involvement in the war increased in Ireland, resulting in the [Conscription Crisis of 1918](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscription_Crisis_of_1918 "Conscription Crisis of 1918").

Other opposition came from [conscientious objectors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscientious_objector "Conscientious objector")—some socialist, some religious—who had refused to fight. In Britain, 16,000 people asked for conscientious objector status.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehmannvan_der_Veer199962_341-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehmannvan_der_Veer199962-341">[324]</a></sup> Some of them, most notably prominent peace activist [Stephen Hobhouse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Hobhouse "Stephen Hobhouse"), refused both military and [alternative service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alternative_civilian_service "Alternative civilian service").<sup id="cite_ref-342"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-342">[325]</a></sup> Many suffered years of prison, including [solitary confinement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solitary_confinement "Solitary confinement") and bread and water diets. Even after the war, in Britain, many job advertisements were marked "No conscientious objectors need to apply".<sup id="cite_ref-343"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-343">[326]</a></sup>

On 1–4 May 1917, about 100,000 workers and soldiers of [Petrograd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Petersburg "Saint Petersburg"), and after them, the workers and soldiers of other Russian cities, led by the Bolsheviks, demonstrated under banners reading "Down with the war!" and "all power to the Soviets!". The mass demonstrations resulted in a crisis for the [Russian Provisional Government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government "Russian Provisional Government").<sup id="cite_ref-344"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-344">[327]</a></sup> In [Milan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milan "Milan"), in May 1917, Bolshevik revolutionaries organised and engaged in rioting calling for an end to the war, and managed to close down factories and stop public transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-Seton_6_345-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Seton_6-345">[328]</a></sup> The Italian army was forced to enter Milan with tanks and machine guns to face Bolsheviks and [anarchists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anarchism "Anarchism"), who fought violently until May 23 when the army gained control of the city. Almost 50 people (including three Italian soldiers) were killed and over 800 people were arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-Seton_6_345-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Seton_6-345">[328]</a></sup>

## Technology

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Sopwith_F-1_Camel.jpg/220px-Sopwith_F-1_Camel.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sopwith_F-1_Camel.jpg)

[Royal Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Air_Force "Royal Air Force") [Sopwith Camel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sopwith_Camel "Sopwith Camel"). In April 1917, the average life expectancy of a British pilot on the Western Front was 93 flying hours.<sup id="cite_ref-346"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-346">[329]</a></sup>

World War I began as a clash of 20th-century technology and 19th-century [tactics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_tactics "Military tactics"), with the inevitably large ensuing casualties. By the end of 1917, however, the major armies, now numbering millions of men, had modernised and were making use of telephone, [wireless communication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wireless "Wireless"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHartcup1988154_347-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHartcup1988154-347">[330]</a></sup> [armoured cars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armored_car_(military) "Armored car (military)"), [tanks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tank "Tank") (especially with the advent of the prototype tank, [Little Willie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Little_Willie "Little Willie")), and aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHartcup198882–86_348-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHartcup198882%E2%80%9386-348">[331]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/CapitaineMarcelCourmes1915.png/220px-CapitaineMarcelCourmes1915.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CapitaineMarcelCourmes1915.png)

[Captain Marcel Courmes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcel_Courmes "Marcel Courmes"), pilot of the French 2nd Bombardment, Group GB 2, August 1915

Artillery also underwent a revolution. In 1914, cannons were positioned in the front line and fired directly at their targets. By 1917, [indirect fire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indirect_fire "Indirect fire") with guns (as well as mortars and even machine guns) was commonplace, using new techniques for spotting and ranging, notably, aircraft and the often overlooked [field telephone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Field_telephone "Field telephone").<sup id="cite_ref-349"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-349">[332]</a></sup>

[Fixed-wing aircraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fixed-wing_aircraft "Fixed-wing aircraft") were initially used for [reconnaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconnaissance "Reconnaissance") and [ground attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Close_air_support "Close air support"). To shoot down enemy planes, [anti-aircraft guns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-aircraft_warfare "Anti-aircraft warfare") and [fighter aircraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fighter_aircraft "Fighter aircraft") were developed. [Strategic bombers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strategic_bomber "Strategic bomber") were created, principally by the Germans and British, though the former used [Zeppelins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zeppelin "Zeppelin") as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Cross_1991_350-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Cross_1991-350">[333]</a></sup> Towards the end of the conflict, aircraft carriers were used for the first time, with HMS _Furious_ launching [Sopwith Camels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sopwith_Camel "Sopwith Camel") in a raid to destroy the Zeppelin hangars at [Tønder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T%C3%B8nder "Tønder") in 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECross199156–57_351-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTECross199156%E2%80%9357-351">[334]</a></sup>

## Diplomacy

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Cartoon_for_a_Telegram.jpg/220px-Cartoon_for_a_Telegram.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cartoon_for_a_Telegram.jpg)

1917 political cartoon about the [Zimmermann Telegram](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zimmermann_Telegram "Zimmermann Telegram")

The non-military diplomatic and propaganda interactions among the nations were designed to build support for the cause or to undermine support for the enemy. For the most part, wartime diplomacy focused on five issues: [propaganda campaigns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propaganda_in_World_War_I "Propaganda in World War I"); defining and redefining the war goals, which became harsher as the war went on; luring neutral nations (Italy, Ottoman Empire, Bulgaria, Romania) into the coalition by offering slices of enemy territory; and encouragement by the Allies of nationalistic minority movements inside the Central Powers, especially among Czechs, Poles, and Arabs. In addition, multiple peace proposals were coming from neutrals, or one side or the other; none of them progressed very far.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStevenson1988[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2020]]<sup_class=&quot;noprint_Inline-Template_&quot;_style=&quot;white-space:nowrap;&quot;>&amp;#91;<i>[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|<span_title=&quot;This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2020)&quot;>page&amp;nbsp;needed</span>]]</i>&amp;#93;</sup>_352-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStevenson1988[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2020]]%3Csup_class=%22noprint_Inline-Template_%22_style=%22white-space:nowrap;%22%3E&amp;#91;%3Ci%3E[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|%3Cspan_title=%22This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2020)%22%3Epage&amp;nbsp;needed%3C/span%3E]]%3C/i%3E&amp;#93;%3C/sup%3E-352">[335]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-353"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-353">[336]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-354">[337]</a></sup>

## Legacy and memory

### Memorials

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Sacrario_militare_di_Redipuglia_agosto_2014.JPG/220px-Sacrario_militare_di_Redipuglia_agosto_2014.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sacrario_militare_di_Redipuglia_agosto_2014.JPG)

The Italian [Redipuglia War Memorial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redipuglia_War_Memorial "Redipuglia War Memorial"), which contains the remains of 100,187 soldiers

Memorials were built in thousands of villages and towns. Close to battlefields, those buried in improvised burial grounds were gradually moved to formal graveyards under the care of organisations such as the [Commonwealth War Graves Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonwealth_War_Graves_Commission "Commonwealth War Graves Commission"), the [American Battle Monuments Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Battle_Monuments_Commission "American Battle Monuments Commission"), the [German War Graves Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_War_Graves_Commission "German War Graves Commission"), and [Le Souvenir français](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Le_Souvenir_fran%C3%A7ais "Le Souvenir français"). Many of these graveyards also have monuments to the missing or [unidentified](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Unknown_Soldier "Tomb of the Unknown Soldier") dead, such as the [Menin Gate Memorial to the Missing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menin_Gate "Menin Gate") and the [Thiepval Memorial to the Missing of the Somme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thiepval_Memorial "Thiepval Memorial").<sup id="cite_ref-355"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-355">[338]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-356"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-356">[339]</a></sup>

In 1915, [John McCrae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_McCrae "John McCrae"), a Canadian army doctor, wrote the poem _[In Flanders Fields](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In_Flanders_Fields "In Flanders Fields")_ as a salute to those who perished in the war. Published in [_Punch_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punch_(magazine) "Punch (magazine)") on 8 December 1915, it is still recited today, especially on [Remembrance Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice_Day "Armistice Day") and [Memorial Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memorial_Day "Memorial Day").<sup id="cite_ref-357"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-357">[340]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-358"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-358">[341]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Pagny_le_Chateau_monument_morts_002b.jpg/220px-Pagny_le_Chateau_monument_morts_002b.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Pagny_le_Chateau_monument_morts_002b.jpg)

A typical village [war memorial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_memorial "War memorial") to soldiers killed in World War I

[National World War I Museum and Memorial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_World_War_I_Museum_and_Memorial "National World War I Museum and Memorial") in [Kansas City, Missouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kansas_City,_Missouri "Kansas City, Missouri"), is a memorial dedicated to all Americans who served in World War I. The [Liberty Memorial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_World_War_I_Museum_and_Memorial "National World War I Museum and Memorial") was dedicated on 1 November 1921, when the supreme Allied commanders spoke to a crowd of more than 100,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-kclibrary.org_359-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-kclibrary.org-359">[342]</a></sup>

The UK Government has budgeted substantial resources to [the commemoration of the war during the period 2014 to 2018](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_World_War_centenary "First World War centenary"). The lead body is the [Imperial War Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_War_Museum "Imperial War Museum").<sup id="cite_ref-360"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-360">[343]</a></sup> On 3 August 2014, French President [François Hollande](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande "François Hollande") and German President [Joachim Gauck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joachim_Gauck "Joachim Gauck") together marked [the centenary of Germany's declaration of war on France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centenary_of_the_outbreak_of_World_War_I "Centenary of the outbreak of World War I") by laying the first stone of a memorial in Vieil Armand, known in German as [Hartmannswillerkopf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hartmannswillerkopf "Hartmannswillerkopf"), for French and German soldiers killed in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-HartmannswillerkopfMemorial_361-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-HartmannswillerkopfMemorial-361">[344]</a></sup> During the [Armistice centenary commemorations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice_Day_centenary "Armistice Day centenary"), French President [Emmanuel Macron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmanuel_Macron "Emmanuel Macron") and German Chancellor [Angela Merkel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angela_Merkel "Angela Merkel") visited the site of the signing of the Armistice of Compiègne and unveiled a plaque to reconciliation.<sup id="cite_ref-362"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-362">[345]</a></sup>

### Historiography

> ... "Strange, friend," I said, "Here is no cause to mourn."  
> "None," said the other, "Save the undone years"... 

The first tentative efforts to comprehend the meaning and consequences of [modern warfare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_warfare "Modern warfare") began during the initial phases of the war; this process continued throughout and after the end of hostilities and is still underway more than a century later. Teaching World War I has presented special challenges. When compared with [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), the First World War is often thought to be "a wrong war fought for the wrong reasons"; it lacks the [metanarrative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metanarrative "Metanarrative") of [good versus evil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_and_evil "Good and evil") that characterizes retellings of the Second World War. Lacking recognizable heroes and villains, it is often taught thematically, invoking [tropes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trope_(literature) "Trope (literature)") like the wastefulness of war, the folly of generals and the innocence of soldiers. The complexity of the conflict is mostly obscured by these oversimplifications.<sup id="cite_ref-Neiberg2_364-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Neiberg2-364">[347]</a></sup> [George Kennan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Kennan "George Kennan") referred to the war as the "seminal catastrophe of the 20th century".<sup id="cite_ref-365"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-365">[348]</a></sup>

Historian Heather Jones argues that the [historiography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historiography "Historiography") has been reinvigorated by a cultural turn in the 21st century. Scholars have raised entirely new questions regarding [military occupation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_occupation "Military occupation"), [radicalisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radicalization "Radicalization") of politics, [race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_(human_categorization) "Race (human categorization)"), [medical science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medical_science "Medical science"), [gender](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_history "Gender history") and [mental health](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mental_health "Mental health"). Among the major subjects that historians have long debated regarding the war include: [Why the war began](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historiography_of_the_causes_of_World_War_I "Historiography of the causes of World War I"); why the [Allies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Allies of World War I") won; whether generals were responsible for [high casualty rates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I_casualties "World War I casualties"); how soldiers endured the poor conditions of [trench warfare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trench_warfare "Trench warfare"); and to what extent the civilian [home front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_front_during_World_War_I "Home front during World War I") accepted and endorsed the war effort.<sup id="cite_ref-366"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-366">[349]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-367"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-367">[350]</a></sup>

### Unexploded ordnance

As late as 2007, signs warning visitors to keep off certain paths at battlefield sites like [Verdun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Verdun "Verdun") and [Somme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Somme_(department) "Somme (department)") remained in place as [unexploded ordnance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unexploded_ordnance "Unexploded ordnance") continued to pose a danger. In France and Belgium locals who discover caches of unexploded munitions are assisted by weapons disposal units. In some places, plant life has still not returned to normal.<sup id="cite_ref-Neiberg2_364-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-Neiberg2-364">[347]</a></sup>

## Footnotes

1.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_ref-1 "Jump up")** Russian Empire during 1914–1917, [Russian Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Republic "Russian Republic") during 1917. The [Bolshevik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolsheviks "Bolsheviks") government signed a [separate peace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk "Treaty of Brest-Litovsk") with the Central Powers shortly after their [armed seizure of power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_Revolution "October Revolution"), resulting in a Central Powers victory on the [Eastern Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_I) "Eastern Front (World War I)") of the war, and Russian defeat. However, this peace treaty was nullified by an Allied Powers victory on the [Western Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I) "Western Front (World War I)"), and the end of the war.
2.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_ref-2 "Jump up")** The United States did not ratify any of the treaties agreed to at the [Paris Peace Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919 "Paris Peace Conference, 1919").
3.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_ref-3 "Jump up")** Bulgaria joined the Central Powers on 14 October 1915.
4.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_ref-4 "Jump up")** The Ottoman Empire agreed to a secret alliance with Germany on 2 August 1914. It joined the war on the side of the Central Powers on 29 October 1914.

13.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_ref-173 "Jump up")** Bessarabia remained part of Romania until 1940, when it was annexed by [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin") as the [Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic");<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERothschild1975314_172-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_note-FOOTNOTERothschild1975314-172">[160]</a></sup> following the dissolution of the USSR in 1991, it became the independent Republic of [Moldova](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moldova "Moldova")
14.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I#cite_ref-230 "Jump up")** Unlike the others, the successor state to the Russian Empire, the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics, retained similar external borders, via retaining or quickly recovering lost territories.
